Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2016</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Structural_Trap_(Anticlinal).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Structural_Trap_%28Anticlinal%29.svg/220px-Structural_Trap_%28Anticlinal%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Structural_Trap_%28Anticlinal%29.svg/330px-Structural_Trap_%28Anticlinal%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Structural_Trap_%28Anticlinal%29.svg/440px-Structural_Trap_%28Anticlinal%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Structural_Trap_(Anticlinal).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A hydrocarbon trap consists of a reservoir rock (yellow) where oil (red) can accumulate, and a caprock (green) that prevents it from egressing.</div></div></div>
<p>Three conditions must be present for oil reservoirs to form:
</p>
<ul><li>a <a href="/wiki/Source_rock" title="Source rock">source rock</a> rich in <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a> material buried deeply enough for subterranean heat to cook it into oil,</li>
<li>a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porous" title="Porous">porous</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permeability_(fluid)" title="Permeability (fluid)">permeable</a> reservoir rock where it can accumulate,</li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Caprock" title="Caprock">caprock</a> (seal) or other mechanism to prevent the oil from escaping to the surface. Within these reservoirs, fluids will typically organize themselves like a three-layer cake with a layer of water below the oil layer and a layer of gas above it, although the different layers vary in size between reservoirs. Because most hydrocarbons are less dense than rock or <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a>, they often migrate upward through adjacent rock layers until either reaching the surface or becoming trapped within porous rocks (known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_reservoir" title="Oil reservoir">reservoirs</a>) by impermeable rocks above. However, the process is influenced by underground water flows, causing oil to migrate hundreds of kilometres horizontally or even short distances downward before becoming trapped in a reservoir. When hydrocarbons are concentrated in a trap, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_field" title="Oil field">oil field</a> forms, from which the liquid can be extracted by <a href="/wiki/Drill" title="Drill">drilling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pump" title="Pump">pumping</a>.</li></ul>
<p>The reactions that produce oil and natural gas are often modeled as first order breakdown reactions, where hydrocarbons are broken down to oil and natural gas by a set of parallel reactions, and oil eventually breaks down to natural gas by another set of reactions. The latter set is regularly used in <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemical</a> plants and <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refineries</a>.
</p><p>Petroleum has mostly been recovered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_drilling" title="Oil drilling">oil drilling</a> (natural petroleum springs are rare). Drilling is carried out after studies of structural geology (at the reservoir scale), sedimentary basin analysis, and reservoir characterisation (mainly in terms of the <a href="/wiki/Porosity" title="Porosity">porosity</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permeability_(earth_sciences)" title="Permeability (earth sciences)">permeability</a> of geologic reservoir structures).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Recent improvements to technologies have also led to exploitation of other unconventional reserves such as <a href="/wiki/Oil_sands" title="Oil sands">oil sands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a>. Wells are drilled into oil reservoirs to extract the crude oil. "Natural lift" production methods that rely on the natural reservoir pressure to force the oil to the surface are usually sufficient for a while after reservoirs are first tapped. In some reservoirs, such as in the Middle East, the natural pressure is sufficient over a long time. The natural pressure in most reservoirs, however, eventually dissipates. Then the oil must be extracted using "<a href="/wiki/Artificial_lift" title="Artificial lift">artificial lift</a>" means. Over time, these "primary" methods become less effective and "secondary" production methods may be used. A common secondary method is <a href="/wiki/Water_injection_(oil_production)" title="Water injection (oil production)">"waterflood"</a> or injection of water into the reservoir to increase pressure and force the oil to the drilled shaft or "wellbore." Eventually "tertiary" or "enhanced" oil recovery methods may be used to increase the oil's flow characteristics by injecting steam, carbon dioxide and other gases or chemicals into the reservoir. In the United States, primary production methods account for less than 40 percent of the oil produced on a daily basis, secondary methods account for about half, and tertiary recovery the remaining 10 percent. Extracting oil (or "bitumen") from oil/tar sand and oil shale deposits requires mining the sand or shale and heating it in a vessel or retort, or using "in-situ" methods of injecting heated liquids into the deposit and then pumping the liquid back out saturated with oil.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unconventional_oil_reservoirs">Unconventional oil reservoirs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Unconventional oil reservoirs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Unconventional_oil" title="Unconventional oil">Unconventional oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oil_sands" title="Oil sands">Oil sands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale_reserves" title="Oil shale reserves">Oil shale reserves</a></div>
<p>Oil-eating bacteria <a href="/wiki/Biodegradation" title="Biodegradation">biodegrade</a> oil that has escaped to the surface. <a href="/wiki/Oil_sands" title="Oil sands">Oil sands</a> are reservoirs of partially biodegraded oil still in the process of escaping and being biodegraded, but they contain so much migrating oil that, although most of it has escaped, vast amounts are still present—more than can be found in conventional oil reservoirs. The lighter fractions of the crude oil are destroyed first, resulting in reservoirs containing an extremely heavy form of crude oil, called crude bitumen in Canada, or extra-heavy crude oil in <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. These two countries have the world's largest deposits of oil sands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>On the other hand, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_shales" title="Oil shales">oil shales</a> are source rocks that have not been exposed to heat or pressure long enough to convert their trapped hydrocarbons into crude oil. Technically speaking, oil shales are not always shales and do not contain oil, but are fined-grain sedimentary rocks containing an insoluble organic solid called <a href="/wiki/Kerogen" title="Kerogen">kerogen</a>. The kerogen in the rock can be converted into crude oil using heat and pressure to simulate natural processes. The method has been known for centuries and was patented in 1694 under British Crown Patent No. 330 covering, "A way to extract and make great quantities of pitch, tar, and oil out of a sort of stone." Although oil shales are found in many countries, the United States has the world's largest deposits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lambertson_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lambertson-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Classification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crudes.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="459" decoding="async" height="384" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Crudes.PNG/350px-Crudes.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/eb/Crudes.PNG 1.5x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crudes.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_(crude_oil)" title="Benchmark (crude oil)">marker crudes</a> with their <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a> content (horizontal) and <a href="/wiki/API_gravity" title="API gravity">API gravity</a> (vertical) and relative production quantity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Brent shown as sweeter than WTI, yet most sources claim the opposite. That and other claims in image probably need checking and sourcing. Example: http://www.petroleum.co.uk/benchmarks (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_(crude_oil)" title="Benchmark (crude oil)">Benchmark (crude oil)</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">petroleum industry</a> generally classifies crude oil by the geographic location it is produced in (e.g., <a href="/wiki/West_Texas_Intermediate" title="West Texas Intermediate">West Texas Intermediate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brent_oilfield" title="Brent oilfield">Brent</a>, or <a href="/wiki/DME_Oman_Crude_Oil_Futures_Contract" title="DME Oman Crude Oil Futures Contract">Oman</a>), its <a href="/wiki/API_gravity" title="API gravity">API gravity</a> (an oil industry measure of density), and its sulfur content. Crude oil may be considered <i><a href="/wiki/Light_crude_oil" title="Light crude oil">light</a></i> if it has low density, <i><a href="/wiki/Heavy_crude_oil" title="Heavy crude oil">heavy</a></i> if it has high density, or <i>medium</i> if it has a density between that of <i>light</i> and <i>heavy</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Additionally, it may be referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Sweet_crude_oil" title="Sweet crude oil">sweet</a></i> if it contains relatively little sulfur or <i><a href="/wiki/Sour_crude_oil" title="Sour crude oil">sour</a></i> if it contains substantial amounts of sulfur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>The geographic location is important because it affects transportation costs to the refinery. <i>Light</i> crude oil is more desirable than <i>heavy</i> oil since it produces a higher yield of gasoline, while <i>sweet</i> oil commands a higher price than <i>sour</i> oil because it has fewer environmental problems and requires less refining to meet sulfur standards imposed on fuels in consuming countries. Each crude oil has unique molecular characteristics which are revealed by the use of <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil_assay" title="Crude oil assay">Crude oil assay</a> analysis in petroleum laboratories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Barrel_(unit)" title="Barrel (unit)">Barrels</a> from an area in which the crude oil's molecular characteristics have been determined and the oil has been classified are used as pricing <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_(crude_oil)" title="Benchmark (crude oil)">references</a> throughout the world. Some of the common reference crudes are:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/West_Texas_Intermediate" title="West Texas Intermediate">West Texas Intermediate</a> (WTI), a very high-quality, sweet, light oil delivered at <a href="/wiki/Cushing,_Oklahoma" title="Cushing, Oklahoma">Cushing, Oklahoma</a> for North American oil</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brent_Crude" title="Brent Crude">Brent Blend</a>, consisting of 15 oils from fields in the <a href="/wiki/Brent_oilfield" title="Brent oilfield">Brent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Central_Platform" title="Ninian Central Platform">Ninian</a> systems in the <a href="/wiki/East_Shetland_Basin" title="East Shetland Basin">East Shetland Basin</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>. The oil is landed at <a href="/wiki/Sullom_Voe" title="Sullom Voe">Sullom Voe</a> terminal in <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>. Oil production from Europe, Africa and Middle Eastern oil flowing West tends to be priced off this oil, which forms a <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_(crude_oil)" title="Benchmark (crude oil)">benchmark</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Crude" title="Dubai Crude">Dubai-Oman</a>, used as benchmark for Middle East sour crude oil flowing to the Asia-Pacific region</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tapis_crude" title="Tapis crude">Tapis</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, used as a reference for light Far East oil)</li>
<li>Minas (from <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, used as a reference for heavy Far East oil)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/OPEC_Reference_Basket" title="OPEC Reference Basket">OPEC Reference Basket</a>, a weighted average of oil blends from various <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> (The Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries) countries</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Midway-Sunset_Oil_Field" title="Midway-Sunset Oil Field">Midway Sunset</a> Heavy, by which heavy oil in California is priced<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (March 2018)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Western_Canadian_Select" title="Western Canadian Select">Western Canadian Select</a> the benchmark crude oil for emerging heavy, high TAN (acidic) crudes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRCPetroleumProducts_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRCPetroleumProducts-90">[90]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>There are declining amounts of these benchmark oils being produced each year, so other oils are more commonly what is actually delivered. While the reference price may be for West Texas Intermediate delivered at Cushing, the actual oil being traded may be a discounted Canadian heavy oil—Western Canadian Select—delivered at <a href="/wiki/Hardisty,_Alberta" title="Hardisty, Alberta">Hardisty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, and for a Brent Blend delivered at Shetland, it may be a discounted Russian Export Blend delivered at the port of <a href="/wiki/Primorsk,_Leningrad_Oblast" title="Primorsk, Leningrad Oblast">Primorsk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>Once extracted, oil is refined and separated, most easily by <a href="/wiki/Continuous_distillation#Continuous_distillation_of_crude_oil" title="Continuous distillation">distillation</a>, into numerous products for direct use or use in manufacturing, such as <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> (petrol), <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a> to <a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">asphalt</a> and chemical <a href="/wiki/Reagent" title="Reagent">reagents</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ethylene" title="Ethylene">ethylene</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propene" title="Propene">propylene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butene" title="Butene">butene</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Acrylic_acid" title="Acrylic acid">acrylic acid</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/P-Xylene" title="P-Xylene">para-xylene</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>) used to make <a href="/wiki/Plastic" title="Plastic">plastics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dixie_State_College_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dixie_State_College-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">Petroleum industry</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Petroleum_industry&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oil_Reserves.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="819" data-file-width="1799" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Oil_Reserves.png/400px-Oil_Reserves.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Oil_Reserves.png/600px-Oil_Reserves.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Oil_Reserves.png/800px-Oil_Reserves.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oil_Reserves.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a>, 2013.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">petroleum industry</a>, also known as the oil industry or the oil patch, includes the global processes of <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">exploration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">extraction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">refining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_transport" title="Petroleum transport">transportation</a> (often by <a href="/wiki/Oil_tanker" title="Oil tanker">oil tankers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_transport" title="Pipeline transport">pipelines</a>), and marketing of <a href="/wiki/List_of_crude_oil_products" title="List of crude oil products">petroleum products</a>. The largest volume products of the industry are <a href="/wiki/Fuel_oil" title="Fuel oil">fuel oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> (petrol). Petroleum is also the raw material for many <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">chemical products</a>, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_drug" title="Pharmaceutical drug">pharmaceuticals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solvent" title="Solvent">solvents</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a>, synthetic <a href="/wiki/Aroma_compound" title="Aroma compound">fragrances</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plastic" title="Plastic">plastics</a>.  The industry is usually divided into three major components: <a href="/wiki/Upstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Upstream (petroleum industry)">upstream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midstream" title="Midstream">midstream</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Downstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Downstream (petroleum industry)">downstream</a>. Upstream regards exploration and extraction of crude oil, midstream encompasses transportation and <a href="/wiki/Oil_terminal" title="Oil terminal">storage</a> of crude, and downstream concerns refining crude oil into various <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_product" title="Petroleum product">end products</a>.
</p><p>Petroleum is vital to many industries, and is necessary for the maintenance of industrial <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a> in its current configuration, making it a critical concern for many nations. Oil accounts for a large percentage of the world’s <a href="/wiki/Energy_consumption" title="Energy consumption">energy consumption</a>, ranging from a low of 32% for <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, to a high of 53% for the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.
</p><p>Other geographic regions' consumption patterns are as follows: <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> (44%), <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> (41%), and <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> (40%). The world consumes 36 billion <a href="/wiki/Barrel_(unit)" title="Barrel (unit)">barrels</a> (5.8 km³) of oil per year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> with developed nations being the largest consumers. The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> consumed 18% of the oil produced in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The production, distribution, refining, and retailing of petroleum taken as a whole represents the world's largest industry in terms of dollar value.
</p><p>The oil and gas industry spends only 0,4% of its net sales for Research &amp; Development which is in comparison with a range of other industries the lowest share.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>Governments such as the United States government provide a heavy public <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_subsidies#Impact_of_fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Energy subsidies">subsidy to petroleum companies</a>, with major tax breaks at various stages of oil exploration and extraction, including the costs of oil field leases and drilling equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Petroleum_industry_nytimes.com_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Petroleum_industry_nytimes.com-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
In recent years, <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_oil_recovery" title="Enhanced oil recovery">enhanced oil recovery</a> techniques — most notably multi-stage drilling and <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_fracturing" title="Hydraulic fracturing">hydraulic fracturing</a> ("fracking") — have moved to the forefront of the industry as this new technology plays a crucial and controversial role in new methods of oil extraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_transport" title="Petroleum transport">Petroleum transport</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Petroleum_transport&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<a href="/wiki/Petroleum_transport" title="Petroleum transport">Petroleum transport</a> is the transportation of petroleum and derivatives such as gasoline (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrol" title="Petrol">petrol</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>  Petroleum products are transported via rail cars, trucks, tanker vessels, and pipeline networks. The method used to move the petroleum products depends on the volume that is being moved and its destination. Even the modes of transportation on land such as pipeline or rail have their own strengths and weaknesses.  One of the key differences are the costs associated with transporting petroleum though pipeline or rail. The biggest problems with moving petroleum products are pollution related and the chance of spillage. Petroleum oil is very hard to clean up and is very toxic to living animals and their surroundings.</div></div>
<p>In the 1950s, shipping costs made up 33 percent of the price of oil transported from the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> to the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist.com_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-104">[104]</a></sup> but due to the development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supertankers" title="Supertankers">supertankers</a> in the 1970s, the cost of shipping dropped to only 5 percent of the price of Persian oil in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist.com_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-104">[104]</a></sup> Due to the increase of the value of the crude oil during the last 30 years, the share of the shipping cost on the final cost of the delivered commodity was less than 3% in 2010.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Price">Price</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Price">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1155" data-file-width="1764" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png/220px-Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png/330px-Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png/440px-Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crude_oil_prices_since_1861.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nominal and inflation-adjusted US dollar price of crude oil, 1861–2015.</div></div></div><div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Price_of_oil" title="Price of oil">Price of oil</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Price_of_oil&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2022</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Cleanup_reorganize plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Ambox rewrite.svg" data-file-height="620" data-file-width="620" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ambox_rewrite.svg/40px-Ambox_rewrite.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ambox_rewrite.svg/60px-Ambox_rewrite.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ambox_rewrite.svg/80px-Ambox_rewrite.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>may be in need of reorganization to comply with Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">layout guidelines</a></b>. The reason given is: <b>Overwhelming amount of information.</b><span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit">editing the article</a> to make improvements to the overall structure.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WTI_crude_oil.webp"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1925" data-file-width="5148" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/WTI_crude_oil.webp/325px-WTI_crude_oil.webp.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/WTI_crude_oil.webp/488px-WTI_crude_oil.webp.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/WTI_crude_oil.webp/650px-WTI_crude_oil.webp.png 2x" width="325"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WTI_crude_oil.webp" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/West_Texas_Intermediate" title="West Texas Intermediate">WTI</a> crude oil price</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2580" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg/220px-A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg/330px-A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg/440px-A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A1_Houston_Office_Oil_Traders_on_Monday.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oil traders, Houston, 2009</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="912" data-file-width="1560" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png/220px-Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png/330px-Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png/440px-Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Graph_price_of_oil_1861_to_2020_WID_data.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nominal_price" title="Nominal price">Nominal price</a> of oil from 1861 to 2020 from <a href="/wiki/Our_World_in_Data" title="Our World in Data">Our World in Data</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Price_of_oil" title="Price of oil">price of oil</a>, or the oil price, generally refers to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spot_price" title="Spot price">spot price</a> of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_barrel" title="Oil barrel">barrel</a> (159 litres) of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benchmark_crude_oil" title="Benchmark crude oil">benchmark crude oil</a>—a reference price for buyers and sellers of crude oil such as <a href="/wiki/West_Texas_Intermediate" title="West Texas Intermediate">West Texas Intermediate</a> (WTI), <a href="/wiki/Brent_Crude" title="Brent Crude">Brent Crude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Crude" title="Dubai Crude">Dubai Crude</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPEC_Reference_Basket" title="OPEC Reference Basket">OPEC Reference Basket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapis_crude" title="Tapis crude">Tapis crude</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonny_Light" title="Bonny Light">Bonny Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urals_oil" title="Urals oil">Urals oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isthmus-34_Light" title="Isthmus-34 Light">Isthmus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Canadian_Select" title="Western Canadian Select">Western Canadian Select</a> (WCS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_Benchmarks_2011_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_Benchmarks_2011-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_pricingdifferences_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_pricingdifferences-106">[106]</a></sup> Oil prices are determined by global supply and demand, rather than any country's domestic production level.
</p><p>The global price of crude oil was relatively consistent in the nineteenth century and early twentieth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_WID_Ritchie_20171002_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_WID_Ritchie_20171002-107">[107]</a></sup> This changed in the 1970s, with a significant increase in the price of oil globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_WID_Ritchie_20171002_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_WID_Ritchie_20171002-107">[107]</a></sup> 
There have been a number of structural drivers of global oil prices historically, including oil supply, demand, and storage shocks, and shocks to global economic growth affecting oil prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_BoC_2019_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_BoC_2019-108">[108]</a></sup> 
Notable events driving significant price fluctuations include the 1973 <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Arab_Petroleum_Exporting_Countries" title="Organization of Arab Petroleum Exporting Countries">OPEC</a> oil <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embargo" title="Embargo">embargo</a> targeting nations that had supported Israel during the <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">Yom Kippur War</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 329">: 329 </span></sup> resulting in the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Iranian Revolution</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1979_oil_crisis" title="1979 oil crisis">1979 oil crisis</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">financial crisis of 2007–2008</a>, and the more recent 2013 <a href="/wiki/2010s_oil_glut" title="2010s oil glut">oil supply glut</a> that led to the "largest oil price declines in modern history" in 2014 to 2016. The 70% decline in global oil prices was "one of the three biggest declines since World War II, and the longest lasting since the supply-driven collapse of 1986."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> 
By 2015, the United States had become the 3rd largest producer of oil—moving from importer to exporter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_CIA_2015_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_CIA_2015-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
The <a href="/wiki/2020_Russia%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_oil_price_war" title="2020 Russia–Saudi Arabia oil price war">2020 Russia–Saudi Arabia oil price war</a> resulted in a 65% decline in global oil prices at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_JPT_Jacobs_2020_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_JPT_Jacobs_2020-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_OECD_2020_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_OECD_2020-113">[113]</a></sup> In 2021, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2021_global_energy_crisis" title="2021 global energy crisis">record-high energy prices</a> were driven by a global surge in demand as the world recovered from the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_recession" title="COVID-19 recession">COVID-19 recession</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_Al-Jazeera_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_Al-Jazeera-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_oil_CNBC_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price_of_oil_CNBC-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> By December 2021, an unexpected rebound in the demand for oil from United States, China and India, coupled with U.S. shale industry investors' "demands to hold the line on spending", has contributed to "tight" oil inventories globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> On 18 January 2022, as the price of Brent crude oil reached its highest since 2014—$88, concerns were raised about the rising cost of gasoline—which hit a record high in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade">Trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Crude oil is traded as a future on the Nymex exchange. Futures contracts are agreements in which buyers and sellers agree to purchase and deliver specific amounts of physical crude oil on a given date in the future. Each contract covers 1000 barrels and can be purchased up to nine years into the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-119">[119]</a></sup> Below are the contract specifications for crude oil:
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_product" title="Petroleum product">Petroleum product</a></div>
<p>The chemical structure of petroleum is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heterogeneity" title="Heterogeneity">heterogeneous</a>, composed of hydrocarbon chains of different lengths. Because of this, petroleum may be taken to <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refineries</a> and the hydrocarbon chemicals separated by <a href="/wiki/Distillation" title="Distillation">distillation</a> and treated by other <a href="/wiki/Chemical_process" title="Chemical process">chemical processes</a>, to be used for a variety of purposes. The total cost per plant is about 9 billion dollars.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuels">Fuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fuels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The most common <a href="/wiki/Fractional_distillation" title="Fractional distillation">distillation fractions</a> of petroleum are <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuels</a>. Fuels include (by increasing boiling temperature range):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-61">[61]</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_derivatives">Other derivatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other derivatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Certain types of resultant hydrocarbons may be mixed with other non-hydrocarbons, to create other end products:
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alkenes" title="Alkenes">Alkenes</a> (olefins), which can be manufactured into plastics or other compounds</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lubricant" title="Lubricant">Lubricants</a> (produces light machine oils, <a href="/wiki/Motor_oil" title="Motor oil">motor oils</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grease_(lubricant)" title="Grease (lubricant)">greases</a>, adding <a href="/wiki/Viscosity" title="Viscosity">viscosity</a> stabilizers as required)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wax" title="Wax">Wax</a>, used in the packaging of <a href="/wiki/Frozen_food" title="Frozen food">frozen foods</a>, among others</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">Sulfur</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sulfuric_acid" title="Sulfuric acid">sulfuric acid</a>. These are useful industrial materials. Sulfuric acid is usually prepared as the acid precursor <a href="/wiki/Oleum" title="Oleum">oleum</a>, a byproduct of <a href="/wiki/Hydrodesulfurization" title="Hydrodesulfurization">sulfur removal</a> from fuels.</li>
<li>Bulk <a href="/wiki/Tar" title="Tar">tar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">Asphalt</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Petroleum_coke" title="Petroleum coke">Petroleum coke</a>, used in speciality carbon products or as solid fuel</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paraffin_wax" title="Paraffin wax">Paraffin wax</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aromatic" title="Aromatic">Aromatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemicals</a> to be used as precursors in other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical" title="Chemical">chemical</a> production</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_by_country">Use by country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Use by country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumption">Consumption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Consumption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the US Energy Information Administration (EIA) estimate for 2017, the world consumes 98.8 million barrels of oil each day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OilConsumptionpercapita.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="347" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/OilConsumptionpercapita.png/750px-OilConsumptionpercapita.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/OilConsumptionpercapita.png/1125px-OilConsumptionpercapita.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9a/OilConsumptionpercapita.png 2x" width="750"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OilConsumptionpercapita.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oil consumption per capita (darker colors represent more consumption, gray represents no data) <i>(source: see file description)</i>. <table style="width: 100%; font-size: 1em;"> <tbody><tr> <td valign="top"> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend nowrap"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#800000; color:white;"> </span>  &gt; 0.07</span><br/> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend nowrap"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#a52a2a; <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For oil production by country, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_production" title="List of countries by oil production">List of countries by oil production</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For oil reserves by country, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">List of countries by proven oil reserves</a>.</div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:-moz-fit-content; width:-webkit-fit-content; width:fit-content;"><div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:auto;">
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1039153519">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style><div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" data-graph-id="2a8d57792f0f055ad9f0f7dddd04e070a5ed4a22" style="min-width:400px;min-height:150px"></div></div><div class="thumbcaption">Top oil-producing countries<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIA2_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-EIA2-126">[126]</a></sup></div></div></div></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oil_producing_countries_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1427" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Oil_producing_countries_map.png/750px-Oil_producing_countries_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Oil_producing_countries_map.png/1125px-Oil_producing_countries_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Oil_producing_countries_map.png 2x" width="750"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oil_producing_countries_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">World map with <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_production" title="List of countries by oil production">countries by oil production</a> (information from 2006–2012).</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>In petroleum industry parlance, <i>production</i> refers to the quantity of crude extracted from reserves, not the literal creation of the product.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exportation">Exportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Exportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_exporters" title="Fossil fuel exporters">Fossil fuel exporters</a> and <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a></div>
