<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_effects">Environmental effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Environmental effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_the_petroleum_industry" title="Environmental impact of the petroleum industry">Environmental impact of the petroleum industry</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dieselrainbow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="871" data-file-width="976" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dieselrainbow.jpg/220px-Dieselrainbow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dieselrainbow.jpg/330px-Dieselrainbow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dieselrainbow.jpg/440px-Dieselrainbow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dieselrainbow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Diesel fuel spill on a road.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, about a quarter of annual global <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> is the carbon dioxide from burning petroleum (plus methane leaks from the industry).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[note 1]</a></sup> Along with the burning of coal, petroleum combustion is the largest contributor to the increase in atmospheric CO<sub>2</sub>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup>  Atmospheric CO<sub>2</sub> has risen over the last 150 years to current levels of over 415 <a href="/wiki/Parts-per_notation" title="Parts-per notation">ppmv</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> from the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere#Past_concentration" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth's atmosphere">180–300 ppmv of the prior 800 thousand years</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> The rise in Arctic temperature has reduced the minimum <a href="/wiki/Arctic_ice_pack" title="Arctic ice pack">Arctic ice pack</a> to 4,320,000 km<sup>2</sup> (1,670,000 sq mi), a loss of almost half since satellite measurements started in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="540" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg/220px-Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg/330px-Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg/440px-Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carbonate_system_of_seawater.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seawater acidification.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">Ocean acidification</a> is the increase in the acidity of the Earth's oceans caused by the uptake of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> (CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub>) from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth's atmosphere">atmosphere</a>. This increase in acidity inhibits all marine life—having a greater impact on smaller organisms as well as shelled organisms (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scallops" title="Scallops">scallops</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extraction">Extraction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Extraction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Oil extraction is simply the removal of oil from the reservoir (oil pool). Oil is often recovered as a water-in-oil emulsion, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specialty_chemicals" title="Specialty chemicals">specialty chemicals</a> called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demulsifiers" title="Demulsifiers">demulsifiers</a> are used to separate the oil from water. Oil extraction is costly and often environmentally damaging. Offshore exploration and extraction of oil disturb the surrounding marine environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_spills">Oil spills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Oil spills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">Oil spill</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_oil_spills" title="List of oil spills">List of oil spills</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:234px;max-width:234px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oil-spill.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="240" decoding="async" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Oil-spill.jpg/230px-Oil-spill.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/Oil-spill.jpg 1.5x" width="230"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Kelp after an oil spill.</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oil_Slick_in_the_Timor_Sea_September-2009.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2224" data-file-width="4448" decoding="async" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Oil_Slick_in_the_Timor_Sea_September-2009.jpg/230px-Oil_Slick_in_the_Timor_Sea_September-2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Oil_Slick_in_the_Timor_Sea_September-2009.jpg/345px-Oil_Slick_in_the_Timor_Sea_September-2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Oil_Slick_in_the_Timor_Sea_September-2009.jpg/460px-Oil_Slick_in_the_Timor_Sea_September-2009.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Oil slick from the <a href="/wiki/Montara_oil_spill" title="Montara oil spill">Montara oil spill</a> in the Timor Sea, September, 2009.</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PrestigeVolunteersInGaliciaCoast.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="199" data-file-width="289" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/PrestigeVolunteersInGaliciaCoast.jpg/230px-PrestigeVolunteersInGaliciaCoast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/PrestigeVolunteersInGaliciaCoast.jpg 1.5x" width="230"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Volunteers cleaning up the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Prestige_oil_spill" title="Prestige oil spill">Prestige oil spill</a>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Crude oil and refined fuel <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">spills</a> from <a href="/wiki/Tanker_(ship)" title="Tanker (ship)">tanker ship</a> accidents have damaged natural <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> and human livelihoods in <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a>, France and many <a href="/wiki/List_of_oil_spills" title="List of oil spills">other places</a>.
</p><p>The quantity of oil spilled during accidents has ranged from a few hundred tons to several hundred thousand tons (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill">Deepwater Horizon oil spill</a>, <a href="/wiki/SS_Atlantic_Empress" title="SS Atlantic Empress">SS Atlantic Empress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amoco_Cadiz" title="Amoco Cadiz">Amoco Cadiz</a>). Smaller spills have already proven to have a great impact on ecosystems, such as the <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill"><i>Exxon Valdez</i> oil spill</a>.
</p><p>Oil spills at sea are generally much more damaging than those on land, since they can spread for hundreds of nautical miles in a thin <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_slick" title="Oil slick">oil slick</a> which can cover beaches with a thin coating of oil. This can kill sea birds, mammals, shellfish and other organisms it coats. Oil spills on land are more readily containable if a makeshift earth dam can be rapidly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulldozed" title="Bulldozed">bulldozed</a> around the spill site before most of the oil escapes, and land animals can avoid the oil more easily.
</p><p>Control of oil spills is difficult, requires ad hoc methods, and often a large amount of manpower. The dropping of bombs and incendiary devices from aircraft on the <a href="/wiki/SS_Torrey_Canyon" title="SS Torrey Canyon">SS <i>Torrey Canyon</i></a> wreck produced poor results;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> modern techniques would include pumping the oil from the wreck, like in the <a href="/wiki/Prestige_oil_spill" title="Prestige oil spill"><i>Prestige</i> oil spill</a> or the <a href="/wiki/MV_Erika" title="MV Erika"><i>Erika</i></a> oil spill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>Though crude oil is predominantly composed of various hydrocarbons, certain nitrogen heterocyclic compounds, such as <a href="/wiki/Pyridine" title="Pyridine">pyridine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Picoline" title="Picoline">picoline</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quinoline" title="Quinoline">quinoline</a> are reported as contaminants associated with crude oil, as well as facilities processing oil shale or coal, and have also been found at legacy <a href="/wiki/Creosote" title="Creosote">wood treatment</a> sites. These compounds have a very high water solubility, and thus tend to dissolve and move with water. Certain naturally occurring bacteria, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Micrococcus" title="Micrococcus">Micrococcus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Arthrobacter" title="Arthrobacter">Arthrobacter</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Rhodococcus" title="Rhodococcus">Rhodococcus</a></i> have been shown to degrade these contaminants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>Because petroleum is a naturally occurring substance, its presence in the environment need not be the result of human causes such as accidents and routine activities (<a href="/wiki/Seismology" title="Seismology">seismic</a> exploration, <a href="/wiki/Boring_(earth)" title="Boring (earth)">drilling</a>, extraction, refining and combustion). Phenomena such as <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_seep" title="Petroleum seep">seeps</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tar_pit" title="Tar pit">tar pits</a> are examples of areas that petroleum affects without man's involvement.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tarballs">Tarballs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Tarballs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A tarball is a blob of crude oil (not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Tar" title="Tar">tar</a>, which is a man-made product derived from pine trees or refined from petroleum) which has been weathered after floating in the ocean. Tarballs are an aquatic <a href="/wiki/Pollutant" title="Pollutant">pollutant</a> in most environments, although they can occur naturally, for example in the Santa Barbara Channel of California<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itah_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-itah-146">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hostettler_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-hostettler-147">[146]</a></sup> or in the Gulf of Mexico off Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> Their concentration and features have been used to assess the extent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_spills" title="Oil spills">oil spills</a>. Their composition can be used to identify their sources of origin,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> and tarballs themselves may be dispersed over long distances by deep sea currents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hostettler_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-hostettler-147">[146]</a></sup> They are slowly decomposed by bacteria, including <i><a href="/wiki/Chromobacterium_violaceum" title="Chromobacterium violaceum">Chromobacterium violaceum</a></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cladosporium_resinae&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cladosporium resinae (page does not exist)">Cladosporium resinae</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bacillus_submarinus" title="Bacillus submarinus">Bacillus submarinus</a></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Micrococcus_varians&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Micrococcus varians (page does not exist)">Micrococcus varians</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pseudomonas_aeruginosa" title="Pseudomonas aeruginosa">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</a></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Candida_marina&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Candida marina (page does not exist)">Candida marina</a></i> and <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Saccharomyces_estuari&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Saccharomyces estuari (page does not exist)">Saccharomyces estuari</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itah_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-itah-146">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Whales">Whales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Whales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>James S. Robbins has argued that the advent of petroleum-refined kerosene saved some species of great whales from <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a> by providing an inexpensive substitute for <a href="/wiki/Whale_oil" title="Whale oil">whale oil</a>, thus eliminating the economic imperative for open-boat <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> but others say that fossil fuels increased whaling with most whales being killed in the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternatives">Alternatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Alternatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2018 road transport used 49% of petroleum, aviation 8%, and uses other than energy 17%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">Electric vehicles</a> are the main alternative for road transport and <a href="/wiki/Aviation_biofuel" title="Aviation biofuel">biojet</a> for aviation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> Single-use plastics have a high carbon footprint and may pollute the sea, but as of 2022 the best alternatives are unclear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2022_boycott_of_Russia_and_Belarus" title="2022 boycott of Russia and Belarus">2022 boycott of Russia and Belarus</a></div>
<p>Control of petroleum production has been a significant driver of international relations during much of the 20th and 21st centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-158">[157]</a></sup> Organizations like OPEC have played an outsized role in international politics. Some historians and commentators have called this the "<a href="/wiki/Age_of_Oil" title="Age of Oil">Age of Oil</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-158">[157]</a></sup> With the rise of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> and addressing <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> some commentators expect a realignment of international power away from <a href="/wiki/Petrostate" title="Petrostate">petrostates</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Oil rents are often seen as connected with corruption in political literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> A 2011 study found that oil rents increased corruption in countries with heavy government involvement in the production of oil. The study found "an increase in oil rents significantly increases corruption" and "significantly deteriorates political rights". The researchers noted oil exploitation gave politicians "an incentive to extend civil liberties but reduce political rights in the presence of oil windfalls to evade redistribution and conflict".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict">Conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Oil_war" title="Oil war">oil war</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petro-aggression" title="Petro-aggression">Petro-aggression</a></div>
<p>Petroleum production is tightly linked with conflict:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> whether through direct aggression such as the U.S. invasion of Iraq, trade wars such as <a href="/wiki/2020_Russia%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_oil_price_war" title="2020 Russia–Saudi Arabia oil price war">the 2020 Russia–Saudi Arabia oil price war</a>, or by fueling conflict in regions such as funding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_civil_war" title="Syrian civil war">Syrian civil war</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="OPEC">OPEC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: OPEC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=OPEC&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>The Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries (<a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">OH</span>-pek</i></a>) is an <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organization</a> of 13<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag ref" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="http://www.opec.org/opec_web/en/about_us/25.htm" rel="nofollow">[ref]</a></sup> countries. Founded on 14 September 1960 in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> by the first five members (<a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>), it has, since 1965, been headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, Austria, although Austria is not an OPEC member state. As of September 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the 13 member countries accounted for an estimated 44 percent of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_production" title="List of countries by oil production">global oil production</a> and 81.5 percent of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">the world's proven oil reserves</a>, giving OPEC a major influence on <a href="/wiki/Price_of_oil" title="Price of oil">global oil prices</a> that were previously determined by the so-called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seven_Sisters_(oil_companies)" title="Seven Sisters (oil companies)">Seven Sisters</a>" grouping of multinational oil companies.
</p><p>The formation of OPEC marked a turning point toward <a href="/wiki/Nationalization_of_oil_supplies" title="Nationalization of oil supplies">national sovereignty over natural resources</a>, and OPEC decisions have come to play a prominent role in the global oil market and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_politics" title="Petroleum politics">international relations</a>. The effect can be particularly strong when wars or <a href="/wiki/Civil_disorder" title="Civil disorder">civil disorders</a> lead to extended interruptions in supply. In the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/1970s_energy_crisis" title="1970s energy crisis">restrictions in oil production</a> led to a dramatic rise in oil prices and in the revenue and wealth of OPEC, with long-lasting and far-reaching consequences for the <a href="/wiki/World_economy" title="World economy">global economy</a>. In the 1980s, OPEC began setting <a href="/wiki/Production_quota" title="Production quota">production targets</a> for its member nations; generally, when the targets are reduced, oil prices increase. This has occurred most recently from the organization's 2008 and 2016 decisions to trim oversupply.
</p><p>Economists have characterized OPEC as a textbook example of a <a href="/wiki/Cartel" title="Cartel">cartel</a> that cooperates to reduce <a href="/wiki/Competition_(economics)" title="Competition (economics)">market competition</a>, but one whose consultations are protected by the doctrine of <a href="/wiki/State_immunity" title="State immunity">state immunity under international law</a>. In the 1960s and 1970s, OPEC successfully restructured the global oil production system so that decision-making authority and the vast majority of profits is in the hands of oil-producing countries. Since the 1980s, OPEC has had a limited impact on world oil supply and price stability, as there is frequent cheating by members on their commitments to one another, and as member commitments reflect what they would do even in the absence of OPEC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OPEC_:1_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-OPEC_:1-162">[161]</a></sup>
</p>
Current OPEC members are<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag ref" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="http://www.opec.org/opec_web/en/about_us/25.htm" rel="nofollow">[ref]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> are former OPEC members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> A larger group called OPEC+ was formed in late 2016 to have more control on the global crude oil market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OPEC_open_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-OPEC_open-164">[163]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_production">Future production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Future production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_oil_production.webp"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="824" data-file-width="760" decoding="async" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/World_oil_production.webp/220px-World_oil_production.webp.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/World_oil_production.webp/330px-World_oil_production.webp.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/World_oil_production.webp/440px-World_oil_production.webp.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_oil_production.webp" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World oil production 2011-2022 average barrels per day</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Consumption_function" title="Consumption function">Consumption</a> in the twentieth and twenty-first centuries has been abundantly pushed by automobile sector growth. The <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">1985–2003 oil glut</a> even fueled the sales of low fuel economy vehicles in <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> countries. The 2008 economic crisis seems to have had some impact on the sales of such vehicles; still, in 2008 oil consumption showed a small increase.
</p><p>In 2016 Goldman Sachs predicted lower demand for oil due to emerging economies concerns, especially China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a> (Brasil, Russia, India, China, South Africa) countries might also kick in, as China briefly had the largest automobile market in December 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> In the long term, uncertainties linger; the <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> believes that the OECD countries will push low consumption policies at some point in the future; when that happens, it will definitely curb oil sales, and both OPEC and the <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a> (EIA) kept lowering their 2020 consumption estimates during the past five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> A detailed review of <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> oil projections have revealed that revisions of world oil production, price and investments have been motivated by a combination of demand and supply factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wachtmeister2018_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wachtmeister2018-168">[167]</a></sup> All together, Non-OPEC conventional projections have been fairly stable the last 15 years, while downward revisions were mainly allocated to OPEC. Recent upward revisions are primarily a result of US <a href="/wiki/Tight_oil" title="Tight oil">tight oil</a>.
</p><p>Production will also face an increasingly complex situation; while OPEC countries still have large reserves at low production prices, newly found reservoirs often lead to higher prices; offshore giants such as <a href="/wiki/Tupi_oil_field" title="Tupi oil field">Tupi</a>, Guara and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiber_oilfield" title="Tiber oilfield">Tiber</a> demand high investments and ever-increasing technological abilities. Subsalt reservoirs such as Tupi were unknown in the twentieth century, mainly because the industry was unable to probe them. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enhanced_Oil_Recovery" title="Enhanced Oil Recovery">Enhanced Oil Recovery</a> (EOR) techniques (example: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daqing_Field" title="Daqing Field">DaQing</a>, China<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup>) will continue to play a major role in increasing the world's recoverable oil.
</p><p>The expected availability of petroleum resources has always been around 35 years or even less since the start of the modern exploration. The <a href="/wiki/Oil_constant" title="Oil constant">oil constant</a>, an insider pun in the German industry, refers to that effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>A growing number of divestment campaigns from major funds pushed by newer generations who question the sustainability of petroleum may hinder the financing of future oil prospection and production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peak_oil">Peak oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Peak oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Peak_oil" title="Peak oil">Peak oil</a></div>
<p>Peak oil is a term applied to the projection that future petroleum production (whether for individual oil wells, entire oil fields, whole countries, or worldwide production) will eventually peak and then decline at a similar rate to the rate of increase before the peak as these reserves are exhausted.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The peak of oil discoveries was in 1965, and oil production per year has surpassed oil discoveries every year since 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> However, this does not mean that potential oil production has surpassed oil demand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2022)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>It is difficult to predict the oil peak in any given region, due to the lack of knowledge and/or transparency in accounting of global oil reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> Based on available production data, proponents have previously predicted the peak for the world to be in years 1989, 1995, or 1995–2000. Some of these predictions date from before the recession of the early 1980s, and the consequent lowering in global consumption, the effect of which was to delay the date of any peak by several years. Just as the 1971 U.S. peak in oil production was only clearly recognized after the fact, a peak in world production will be difficult to discern until production clearly drops off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, according to <a href="/wiki/BP#Climate_policy" title="BP">BP's Energy Outlook 2020</a>, peak oil had been reached, due to the changing energy landscape coupled with the <a href="/wiki/Financial_market_impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic#Oil_prices" title="Financial market impact of the COVID-19 pandemic">economic toll of the COVID-19 pandemic</a>.
</p><p>While there has been much focus historically on peak oil supply, focus is increasingly shifting to peak demand as more countries seek to transition to renewable energy. The GeGaLo index of geopolitical gains and losses assesses how the geopolitical position of 156 countries may change if the world fully transitions to renewable energy resources. Former oil exporters are expected to lose power, while the positions of former oil importers and countries rich in renewable energy resources is expected to strengthen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unconventional_oil">Unconventional oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Unconventional oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2022</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Unconventional oil is petroleum produced or extracted using techniques other than the conventional methods. The calculus for peak oil has changed with the introduction of unconventional production methods. In particular, the combination of <a href="/wiki/Directional_drilling" title="Directional drilling">horizontal drilling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_fracturing" title="Hydraulic fracturing">hydraulic fracturing</a> has resulted in a significant increase in production from previously uneconomic plays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> Analysts expected that $150 billion would be spent on further developing North American tight oil fields in 2015. The large increase in tight oil production is one of the reasons behind the price drop in late 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> Certain rock <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strata" title="Strata">strata</a> contain hydrocarbons but have low permeability and are not thick from a vertical perspective. Conventional vertical wells would be unable to economically retrieve these hydrocarbons. Horizontal drilling, extending horizontally through the strata, permits the well to access a much greater volume of the strata. Hydraulic fracturing creates greater permeability and increases hydrocarbon flow to the wellbore.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrocarbons_on_other_worlds">Hydrocarbons on other worlds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Hydrocarbons on other worlds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturn_(planet)" title="Saturn (planet)">Saturn's</a> largest moon, <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>, lakes of liquid hydrocarbons comprising methane, ethane, propane and other constituents, occur naturally. Data collected by the space probe <i><a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini–Huygens">Cassini–Huygens</a></i> yield an estimate that the visible lakes and seas of Titan contain about 300 times the volume of Earth's proven oil reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oil_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-oil-178">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> Drilled samples from the surface of <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> taken in 2015 by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curiosity_Rover" title="Curiosity Rover"><i>Curiosity</i> rover's</a> <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">Mars Science Laboratory</a> have found organic molecules of <a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">benzene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Propane" title="Propane">propane</a> in 3-billion-year-old rock samples in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gale_Crater" title="Gale Crater">Gale Crater</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt20180607_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20180607-180">[179]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_fiction">In fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: In fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Petrofiction" title="Petrofiction">Petrofiction</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Petrofiction&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<a href="/wiki/Petrofiction" title="Petrofiction">Petrofiction</a> or oil fiction,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Petrofiction_:4_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Petrofiction_:4-181">[180]</a></sup> is a genre of fiction focused on the role of petroleum in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Petrofiction_:5_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Petrofiction_:5-182">[181]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petroleum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-176"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-176">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2"><a class="external text" href="http://www.eia.gov/analysis/petroleum/crudetypes/pdf/crudetypes.pdf" rel="nofollow"><i>U.S. Crude Oil Production Forecast – Analysis of Crude Types</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, Washington, DC: U.S. Energy Information Administration, May 28, 2015, <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20191122192224/https://www.eia.gov/analysis/petroleum/crudetypes/pdf/crudetypes.pdf" rel="nofollow">archived</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> from the original on November 22, 2019<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">September 13,</span> 2018</span>, <q>U.S. oil production has grown rapidly in recent years. U.S. Energy Information Administration (EIA) data, which reflect combined production of crude oil and lease condensate, show a rise from 5.6 million barrels per day (bbl/d) in 2011 to 7.5 million bbl/d in 2013, and a record 1.2 million bbl/d increase to 8.7 million bbl/d in 2014. Increasing production of light crude oil in low-permeability or tight resource formations in regions like the Bakken, Permian Basin, and Eagle Ford (often referred to as light tight oil) account for nearly all the net growth in U.S. crude oil production.<br/>EIA’s latest Short-Term Energy Outlook, issued in May 2015, reflects continued production growth in 2015 and 2016, albeit at a slower pace than in 2013 and 2014, with U.S. crude oil production in 2016 forecast to reach 9.2 million bbl/d. Beyond 2016, the Annual Energy Outlook 2015 (AEO2015) projects further production growth, although its pace and duration remains highly uncertain.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=U.S.+Crude+Oil+Production+Forecast+%E2%80%93+Analysis+of+Crude+Types&amp;rft.place=Washington%2C+DC&amp;rft.pub=U.S.+Energy+Information+Administration&amp;rft.date=2015-05-28&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.eia.gov%2Fanalysis%2Fpetroleum%2Fcrudetypes%2Fpdf%2Fcrudetypes.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APetroleum"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-nyt20180607-180"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-nyt20180607_180-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation news cs1" id="CITEREFChang2018">Chang, Kenneth (June 7, 2018). <a class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/07/science/mars-nasa-life.html" rel="nofollow">"Life on Mars?
